## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: thermomechanical constitutive modeling (materials science)
**Analysis**: This task models the stress-strain-temperature relationship in materials, where stress typically increases with strain through elastic response and strain hardening, while increasing temperature causes thermal softening. Classical constitutive models combine these effects multiplicatively or additively.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Hooke's law (linear elastic): sigma = c0 * epsilon (linear stress-strain at small strains)
- Temperature-dependent Hooke's law: sigma = c0 * epsilon * (c1 - c2 * T) (elastic modulus decreasing linearly with temperature)
- Power-law hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 (Hollomon-type strain hardening)
- Ludwik model: sigma = c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2 (yield stress plus power-law hardening)
- Ramberg-Osgood inverse: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**c2 (combined linear and nonlinear strain terms)
- Thermal softening power law: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * T**c2 (power-law coupling of strain hardening and thermal effect)
- Linear thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * (c2 - c3 * T) (power-law hardening with linear thermal softening)
- Johnson-Cook type: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (c3 - c4 * T**c5) (hardening times thermal softening)
- Exponential thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(c2 * T) (Arrhenius-type thermal dependence with hardening)
- Voce hardening with thermal softening: sigma = (c0 - c1 * exp(c2 * epsilon)) * (c3 - c4 * T) (saturating hardening with linear softening)
- Exponential saturation: sigma = c0 * (c1 - exp(c2 * epsilon)) (Voce-type saturating stress-strain curve)
- Combined exponential: sigma = c0 * exp(c1 * epsilon) * exp(c2 * T) (exponential dependence on both variables)
- Polynomial with temperature: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon + c2 * epsilon**2) * (c3 + c4 * T) (polynomial hardening with thermal factor)
- Sinh-based flow stress: sigma = c0 * T * asinh(c1 * epsilon * exp(c2 / T)) (Zener-Hollomon / hyperbolic sine creep model)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Strain hardening saturation → Use (1 - exp(-c*epsilon)) or tanh(c*epsilon) to capture stress saturation at large strains
- Thermal softening as multiplicative factor → Temperature effects often appear as a multiplicative prefactor (1 - T*c) or (T_ref - T)**c on the mechanical response
- Elastic-to-plastic transition → Sum of linear term (c*epsilon) and power-law term (c*epsilon**n with n<1) captures initial stiffness transitioning to hardening
- Arrhenius-type thermal activation → exp(c/T) or exp(-c*T) terms reflect thermally activated dislocation mechanisms in plastic flow
- Yield stress offset → Additive constant c0 representing initial yield stress before strain hardening: sigma = c0 + f(epsilon)
- Modulus-temperature linearity → Elastic modulus (slope of stress-strain) often decreases approximately linearly with temperature in metals below melting
- Homologous temperature scaling → Temperature appears as (T_melt - T) or normalized form, suggesting thermal softening vanishes at melting point
- Strain rate analogy with strain → In quasi-static models, strain and temperature may couple through Boltzmann-type factors epsilon*exp(c/T)
